Although their causes and pathogeneses differ, they are both related to the dysfunction of the middle jiao (spleen and stomach). The lung is the master of qi, and the middle jiao is the source of qi and blood production. If the middle jiao is out of balance, the function of body fluids to carry qi is impeded, leading to the stagnation of lung qi and the onset of whooping cough. If phlegm-dampness is internally generated and accumulates over time to transform into heat, with phlegm and heat intermingling, it can result in a lung abscess. Additionally, cold nature tends to cause stagnation, easily leading to phlegm coagulation in the uterus, affecting the thoroughfare and conception vessels, and thereby causing symptoms such as enuresis and tremor. It can be seen that the dysfunction of the middle jiao plays a significant role in the onset of lung-related diseases and various gynecological disorders. In clinical practice, attention should be paid to regulating and smoothing the middle jiao to restore the function of body fluids carrying qi.

Further analysis shows that patients with bone tuberculosis often present signs of blood stasis, with a lingering disease course. In tongue diagnosis, the appearance of white sticky fur indicates internal obstruction of phlegm-dampness, closely related to the pathogenesis of yin jaundice and wasting jaundice. Yin jaundice is mostly caused by internal accumulation of cold-dampness, while wasting jaundice is often due to weakness of the spleen and stomach, and insufficient generation and transformation of qi and blood. Synthesizing the above syndromes, it is evident that dysfunction of zang-fu organs and stagnation of qi and blood are key factors in pathogenesis, and treatment should focus on harmonizing the spleen and stomach, and promoting blood circulation to remove stasis.

Medications that clear deficiency heat, such as Danpi, can help clear internal heat and harmonize Qi and blood. However, during treatment, it is essential to prevent excessively strong medication properties that may damage vital Qi, and treatment should be based on syndrome differentiation, flexibly adjusted to achieve the effect of addressing both the root cause and symptoms.

Oral canker is often caused by stomach fire and reversed qi syndrome, manifested as oral ulcers, and should be treated by clearing the stomach and reducing fire. Infantile spasmodic cough is usually triggered by kidney deficiency and marrow depletion syndrome, characterized by frequent coughing, and should be treated by tonifying the kidney and enriching the marrow. Additionally, blood stasis blocking the collaterals syndrome plays a significant role in the pathological mechanism of inguinal abscess, presenting with local swelling and pain, and should be treated by activating blood and resolving stasis. The method of regulating qi and expelling phlegm is suitable for the syndrome of qi stagnation and phlegm obstruction, which alleviates symptoms by regulating qi dynamics and resolving phlegm. The symptom of muscle cramps is mostly due to the invasion of cold-dampness, causing muscle and tendon spasms, and should be treated by warming the meridians and dispelling cold, relaxing tendons and activating collaterals. In summary, syndrome differentiation and treatment are particularly important in pediatric diseases, and specific treatments must be applied in conjunction with specific syndrome types to achieve significant therapeutic effects.

For the syndrome of blood stasis obstructing the lung collaterals, it is advisable to combine cough-relieving and asthma-calming herbs to disperse phlegm, ventilate the lungs, unblock collaterals, and dissipate blood stasis. Additionally, although centipede bites are external factors, they also require syndrome differentiation and treatment to prevent pathogenic qi from invading internally and affecting the recovery of vital energy. Comprehensive regulation can address both the root and symptoms, restoring the body's yin-yang balance.

For symptoms of lower consumption, tapping massage can also play an auxiliary role. TCM often speaks of "one source, three branches," indicating that various parts of the body are interconnected, and holistic regulation is necessary. Paying attention to diet and emotional management in daily life is essential for fundamentally improving health status.
